The `ObligationForest` is a utility data structure used in trait\n     2→//! matching to track the set of outstanding obligations (those not yet\n     3→//! resolved to success or error). It also tracks the \"backtrace\" of each\n     4→//! pending obligation (why we are trying to figure this out in the first\n     5→//! place).\n     6→//!\n     7→//! ### External view\n     8→//!\n     9→//! `ObligationForest` supports two main public operations (there are a\n    10→//! few others not discussed here):\n    11→//!\n    12→//! 1. Add a new root obligations (`register_obligation`).\n    13→//! 2. Process the pending obligations (`process_obligations`).\n    14→//!\n    15→//! When a new obligation `N` is added, it becomes the root of an\n    16→//! obligation tree. This tree can also carry some per-tree state `T`,\n    17→//! which is given at the same time. This tree is a singleton to start, so\n    18→//! `N` is both the root and the only leaf. Each time the\n    19→//! `process_obligations` method is called, it will invoke its callback\n    20→//! with every pending obligation (so that will include `N`, the first\n    21→//! time). The callback also receives a (mutable) reference to the\n    22→//! per-tree state `T`. The callback should process the obligation `O`\n    23→//! that it is given and return a `ProcessResult`:\n    24→//!\n    25→//! - `Unchanged` -> ambiguous result. Obligation was neither a success\n    26→//!   nor a failure. It is assumed that further attempts to process the\n    27→//!   obligation will yield the same result unless something in the\n    28→//!   surrounding environment changes.\n    29→//! - `Changed(C)` - the obligation was *shallowly successful*. The\n    30→//!   vector `C` is a list of subobligations. The meaning of this is that\n    31→//!   `O` was successful on the assumption that all the obligations in `C`\n    32→//!   are also successful. Therefore, `O` is only considered a \"true\"\n    33→//!   success if `C` is empty. Otherwise, `O` is put into a suspended\n    34→//!   state and the obligations in `C` become the new pending\n    35→//!   obligations. They will be processed the next time you call\n    36→//!   `process_obligations`.\n    37→//! - `Error(E)` -> obligation failed with error `E`. We will collect this\n    38→//!   error and return it from `process_obligations`, along with the\n    39→//!   \"backtrace\" of obligations (that is, the list of obligations up to\n    40→//!   and including the root of the failed obligation). No further\n    41→//!   obligations from that same tree will be processed, since the tree is\n    42→//!   now considered to be in error.\n    43→//!\n    44→//! When the call to `process_obligations` completes, you get back an `Outcome`,\n    45→//! which includes two bits of information:\n    46→//!\n    47→//! - `completed`: a list of obligations where processing was fully\n    48→//!   completed without error (meaning that all transitive subobligations\n    49→//!   have also been completed). So, for example, if the callback from\n    50→//!   `process_obligations` returns `Changed(C)` for some obligation `O`,\n    51→//!   then `O` will be considered completed right away if `C` is the\n    52→//!   empty vector. Otherwise it will only be considered completed once\n    53→//!   all the obligations in `C` have been found completed.\n    54→//! - `errors`: a list of errors that occurred and associated backtraces\n    55→//!   at the time of error, which can be used to give context to the user.\n    56→//!\n    57→//! Upon completion, none of the existing obligations were *shallowly\n    58→//! successful* (that is, no callback returned `Changed(_)`). This implies that\n    59→//! all obligations were either errors or returned an ambiguous result.\n    60→//!\n    61→//! ### Implementation details\n    62→//!\n    63→//! For the most part, comments specific to the implementation are in the\n    64→//! code. This file only contains a very high-level overview. Basically,\n    65→//! the forest is stored in a vector. Each element of the vector is a node\n    66→//! in some tree. Each node in the vector has the index of its dependents,\n    67→//! including the first dependent which is known as the parent. It also\n    68→//! has a current state, described by `NodeState`. The `ObligationForest` is a utility data structure used in trait\n//! matching to track the set of outstanding obligations (those not yet\n//! resolved to success or error). It also tracks the \"backtrace\" of each\n//! pending obligation (why we are trying to figure this out in the first\n//! place).\n//!\n//! ### External view\n//!\n//! `ObligationForest` supports two main public operations (there are a\n//! few others not discussed here):\n//!\n//! 1. Add a new root obligations (`register_obligation`).\n//! 2. Process the pending obligations (`process_obligations`).\n//!\n//! When a new obligation `N` is added, it becomes the root of an\n//! obligation tree. This tree can also carry some per-tree state `T`,\n//! which is given at the same time. This tree is a singleton to start, so\n//! `N` is both the root and the only leaf. Each time the\n//! `process_obligations` method is called, it will invoke its callback\n//! with every pending obligation (so that will include `N`, the first\n//! time). The callback also receives a (mutable) reference to the\n//! per-tree state `T`. The callback should process the obligation `O`\n//! that it is given and return a `ProcessResult`:\n//!\n//! - `Unchanged` -> ambiguous result. Obligation was neither a success\n//!   nor a failure. It is assumed that further attempts to process the\n//!   obligation will yield the same result unless something in the\n//!   surrounding environment changes.\n//! - `Changed(C)` - the obligation was *shallowly successful*. The\n//!   vector `C` is a list of subobligations. The meaning of this is that\n//!   `O` was successful on the assumption that all the obligations in `C`\n//!   are also successful. Therefore, `O` is only considered a \"true\"\n//!   success if `C` is empty. Otherwise, `O` is put into a suspended\n//!   state and the obligations in `C` become the new pending\n//!   obligations. They will be processed the next time you call\n//!   `process_obligations`.\n//! - `Error(E)` -> obligation failed with error `E`. We will collect this\n//!   error and return it from `process_obligations`, along with the\n//!   \"backtrace\" of obligations (that is, the list of obligations up to\n//!   and including the root of the failed obligation). No further\n//!   obligations from that same tree will be processed, since the tree is\n//!   now considered to be in error.\n//!\n//! When the call to `process_obligations` completes, you get back an `Outcome`,\n//! which includes two bits of information:\n//!\n//! - `completed`: a list of obligations where processing was fully\n//!   completed without error (meaning that all transitive subobligations\n//!   have also been completed). So, for example, if the callback from\n//!   `process_obligations` returns `Changed(C)` for some obligation `O`,\n//!   then `O` will be considered completed right away if `C` is the\n//!   empty vector. Otherwise it will only be considered completed once\n//!   all the obligations in `C` have been found completed.\n//! - `errors`: a list of errors that occurred and associated backtraces\n//!   at the time of error, which can be used to give context to the user.\n//!\n//! Upon completion, none of the existing obligations were *shallowly\n//! successful* (that is, no callback returned `Changed(_)`). This implies that\n//! all obligations were either errors or returned an ambiguous result.\n//!\n//! ### Implementation details\n//!\n//! For the most part, comments specific to the implementation are in the\n//! code. This file only contains a very high-level overview. Basically,\n//! the forest is stored in a vector. Each element of the vector is a node\n//! in some tree. Each node in the vector has the index of its dependents,\n//! including the first dependent which is known as the parent. It also\n//! has a current state, described by `NodeState`. After each processing\n//! step, we compress the vector to remove completed and error nodes, which\n//! aren't needed anymore.\n\nuse std::cell::Cell;\nuse std::collections::hash_map::Entry;\nuse std::fmt::Debug;\nuse std::hash;\nuse std::marker::PhantomData;\n\nuse thin_vec::ThinVec;\nuse tracing::debug;\n\nuse crate::fx::{FxHashMap, FxHashSet};\n\nmod graphviz;\n\n#[cfg(test)]\nmod tests;\n\npub trait ForestObligation: Clone + Debug {\n    type CacheKey: Clone + hash::Hash + Eq + Debug;\n\n    /// Converts this `ForestObligation` suitable for use as a cache key.\n    /// If two distinct `ForestObligations`s return the same cache key,\n    /// then it must be sound to use the result of processing one obligation\n    /// (e.g. success for error) for the other obligation\n    fn as_cache_key(&self) -> Self::CacheKey;\n}\n\npub trait ObligationProcessor {\n    type Obligation: ForestObligation;\n    type Error: Debug;","numLines":100,"startLine":1,"totalLines":743}}}

Otherwise, the `match` appearing\n// in `process_obligations` is significantly slower, which can substantially affect\n// benchmarks like `rustc-perf`'s inflate and keccak.\n#[repr(C)]\n#[derive(Debug)]\npub enum ProcessResult<O, E> {\n    Unchanged,\n    Changed(ThinVec<O>),\n    Error(E),\n}\n\n#[derive(Clone, Copy, PartialEq, Eq, Hash, Debug)]\nstruct ObligationTreeId(usize);\n\npub struct ObligationForest<O: ForestObligation> {\n    /// The list of obligations. In between calls to [Self::process_obligations],\n    /// this list only contains nodes in the `Pending` or `Waiting` state.\n    ///\n    /// `usize` indices are used here and throughout this module, rather than\n    /// [`rustc_index::newtype_index!`] indices, because this code is hot enough\n    /// that the `u32`-to-`usize` conversions that would be required are\n    /// significant, and space considerations are not important.\n    nodes: Vec<Node<O>>,\n\n    /// A cache of predicates that have been successfully completed.\n    done_cache: FxHashSet<O::CacheKey>,\n\n    /// A cache of the nodes in `nodes`, indexed by predicate. Unfortunately,\n    /// its contents are not guaranteed to match those of `nodes`. See the\n    /// comments in `Self::process_obligation` for details.\n    active_cache: FxHashMap<O::CacheKey, usize>,\n\n    /// A vector reused in [Self::compress()] and [Self::find_cycles_from_node()],\n    /// to avoid allocating new vectors.\n    reused_node_vec: Vec<usize>,\n\n    obligation_tree_id_generator: ObligationTreeIdGenerator,\n\n    /// Per tree error cache. This is used to deduplicate errors,\n    /// which is necessary to avoid trait resolution overflow in\n    /// some cases.\n    ///\n    /// See [this][details] for details.\n    ///\n    /// [details]: https://github.com/rust-lang/rust/pull/53255#issuecomment-421184780\n    error_cache: FxHashMap<ObligationTreeId, FxHashSet<O::CacheKey>>,\n}\n\n#[derive(Debug)]\nstruct Node<O> {\n    obligation: O,\n    state: Cell<NodeState>,\n\n    /// Obligations that depend on this obligation for their completion. They\n    /// must all be in a non-pending state.\n    dependents: Vec<usize>,\n\n    /// If true, `dependents[0]` points to a \"parent\" node, which requires\n    /// special treatment upon error but is otherwise treated the same.\n    /// (It would be more idiomatic to store the parent node in a separate\n    /// `Option<usize>` field, but that slows down the common case of\n    /// iterating over the parent and other descendants together.)\n    has_parent: bool,\n\n    /// Identifier of the obligation tree to which this node belongs.\n    obligation_tree_id: ObligationTreeId,\n}\n\nimpl<O> Node<O> {\n    fn new(parent: Option<usize>, obligation: O, obligation_tree_id: ObligationTreeId) -> Node<O> {\n        Node {\n            obligation,\n            state: Cell::new(NodeState::Pending),\n            dependents: if let Some(parent_index) = parent { vec![parent_index] } else { vec![] },\n            has_parent: parent.is_some(),\n            obligation_tree_id,\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n/// The state of one node in some tree within the forest. This represents the\n/// current state of processing for the obligation (of type `O`) associated\n/// with this node.\n///\n/// The non-`Error` state transitions are as follows.\n/// ```text\n/// (Pre-creation)\n///  |\n///  |     register_obligation_at() (called by process_obligations() and\n///  v                               from outside the crate)\n/// Pending\n///  |\n///  |     process_obligations()\n///  v\n/// Success\n///  |  ^\n///  |  |  mark_successes()\n///  |  v\n///  |  Waiting\n///  |\n///  |     process_cycles()\n///  v\n/// Done\n///  |\n///  |     compress()\n///  v\n/// (Removed)\n/// ```\n/// The `Error` state can be introduced in several places, via `error_at()`.\n///\n/// Outside of `ObligationForest` methods, nodes should be either `Pending` or\n/// `Waiting`.\n#[derive(Debug, Copy, Clone, PartialEq, Eq)]\nenum NodeState {\n    /// This obligation has not yet been selected successfully. Cannot have\n    /// subobligations.\n    Pending,\n\n    /// This obligation was selected successfully, but may or may not have\n    /// subobligations.\n    Success,\n\n    /// This obligation was selected successfully, but it has a pending\n    /// subobligation.\n    Waiting,\n\n    /// This obligation, along with its subobligations, are complete, and will\n    /// be removed in the next collection.\n    Done,\n\n    /// This obligation was resolved to an error. It will be removed by the\n    /// next compression step.\n    Error,\n}\n\n/// This trait allows us to have two different Outcome types:\n///  - the normal one that does as little as possible\n///  - one for tests that does some additional work and checking\npub trait OutcomeTrait {\n    type Error;\n    type Obligation;\n\n    fn new() -> Self;\n    fn record_completed(&mut self, outcome: &Self::Obligation);\n    fn record_error(&mut self, error: Self::Error);\n}\n\n#[derive(Debug)]\npub struct Outcome<O, E> {\n    /// Backtrace of obligations that were found to be in error.\n    pub errors: Vec<Error<O, E>>,\n}\n\nimpl<O, E> OutcomeTrait for Outcome<O, E> {\n    type Error = Error<O, E>;\n    type Obligation = O;\n\n    fn new() -> Self {\n        Self { errors: vec![] }\n    }\n\n    fn record_completed(&mut self, _outcome: &Self::Obligation) {","numLines":200,"startLine":100,"totalLines":743}}}

Matching is\n/// intended to be used only on freshened types, and it basically\n/// indicates if the non-freshened versions of A and B could have been\n/// unified.\n///\n/// It is only an approximation. [rustc-dev-guide]: https://rustc-dev-guide.rust-lang.org/traits/resolution.html\n     4→\n     5→mod engine;\n     6→mod project;\n     7→mod structural_impls;\n     8→pub mod util;\n     9→\n    10→use std::cmp;\n    11→use std::hash::{Hash, Hasher};\n    12→\n    13→use hir::def_id::LocalDefId;\n    14→use rustc_hir as hir;\n    15→use rustc_macros::{TypeFoldable, TypeVisitable};\n    16→use rustc_middle::traits::query::NoSolution;\n    17→use rustc_middle::traits::solve::Certainty;\n    18→pub use rustc_middle::traits::*;\n    19→use rustc_middle::ty::{self, Ty, TyCtxt, Upcast};\n    20→use rustc_span::Span;\n    21→use thin_vec::ThinVec;\n    22→\n    23→pub use self::engine::{FromSolverError, ScrubbedTraitError, TraitEngine};\n    24→pub(crate) use self::project::UndoLog;\n    25→pub use self::project::{\n    26→    MismatchedProjectionTypes, Normalized, NormalizedTerm, ProjectionCache, ProjectionCacheEntry,\n    27→    ProjectionCacheKey, ProjectionCacheStorage,\n    28→};\n    29→use crate::infer::InferCtxt;\n    30→\n    31→/// An `Obligation` represents some trait reference (e.g., `i32: Eq`) for\n    32→/// which the \"impl_source\" must be found. The process of finding an \"impl_source\" is\n    33→/// called \"resolving\" the `Obligation`. This process consists of\n    34→/// either identifying an `impl` (e.g., `impl Eq for i32`) that\n    35→/// satisfies the obligation, or else finding a bound that is in\n    36→/// scope. solver implements a sophisticated system for resolving trait bounds and detecting unsatisfied trait constraints. The system follows a pipeline architecture with clear separation of concerns.\\n\\n## Obligation Forest Foundation\\nThe `ObligationForest` (compiler/rustc_data_structures/src/obligation_forest/mod.rs) provides the core data structure for managing trait obligations. It maintains a forest of obligation trees where each node represents a pending obligation. The forest supports three processing results: Unchanged (ambiguous), Changed with sub-obligations, and Error. The state machine includes states: Pending -> Success -> Waiting -> Done, or Error. This enables efficient batch processing while tracking obligation dependencies.\\n\\n## Fulfillment and Obligation Registration\\nThe `FulfillmentContext` (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/fulfill.rs) wraps the ObligationForest for the old trait solver. When obligations are registered via `ObligationCtxt::register_obligation` (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/engine.rs), they become `PendingPredicateObligation` nodes containing the predicate, parameter environment, and recursion depth. The context implements `ObligationProcessor` to handle obligation processing callbacks.\\n\\n## Trait Selection Pipeline\\nThe `SelectionContext` (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/mod.rs) is the central orchestrator for trait resolution. The selection process follows a well-defined pipeline:\\n\\n1. **Candidate Assembly**: The `assemble_candidates` method (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/candidate_assembly.rs) gathers all possible trait implementations from:\\n   - Trait aliases\\n   - User-defined implementations\\n   - Caller bounds and where-clauses\\n   - Builtin implementations (Copy, Clone, Sized, etc.)\\n   - Auto-traits\\n   - Projection candidates (associated types)\\n\\n2. **Matching**: The `MatchAgainstFreshVars` type relation (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/_match.rs) tests whether candidate trait references match the obligation. It performs type unification on freshened types to determine if an impl could satisfy the obligation.\\n\\n3. **Confirmation**: The `confirm_candidate` method (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/confirmation.rs) unifies the trait reference with the obligation and produces an `ImplSource` that represents the selected implementation. For user-defined impls, it recursively generates sub-obligations for where-clause bounds.\\n\\n## Specialization and Impl Matching\\nThe specialization system (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/specialize/mod.rs) enforces impl consistency rules. The `OverlapError` structure handles cases where multiple impls could apply. The specialization graph (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/specialize/specialization_graph.rs) organizes impls by their specificity, ensuring that more specific implementations take precedence.\\n\\n## Associated Type Projection\\nThe projection system (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/project.rs) resolves associated types during trait selection. It defines `ProjectionObligation` types and `ProjectionCandidate` sources including parameter environment bounds, trait definitions, object types, and selections. This system integrates with the main trait solver to handle complex generic types with associated type constraints.\\n\\n## Error Reporting\\nWhen obligations cannot be satisfied, the error reporting system provides detailed diagnostics:\\n\\n- `report_selection_error` (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/error_reporting/traits/fulfillment_errors.rs) generates the primary error message, handling multiple error categories including Unimplemented, Unsupported, and TraitNotObjectSafe\\n- The error reporting context (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/error_reporting/traits/mod.rs) manages candidate similarity analysis and provides contextual information\\n- The suggestions module (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/error_reporting/traits/suggestions.rs) offers actionable fixes\\n\\n## Type System Integration\\nThe trait system integrates with the broader type system through several key types:\\n\\n- `ObligationCause` (compiler/rustc_middle/src/traits/mod.rs) provides attribution for why obligations exist, including the source span and obligation cause code\\n- `FulfillmentError` tracks failed obligations with their error codes and root cause information\\n- `Obligation<T>` (compiler/rustc_infer/src/traits/mod.rs) is the generic container for any goal to prove, including recursion depth tracking for termination\\n\\nThe unified interface allows the same machinery to handle trait predicates, projection predicates, and well-formedness constraints. When obligations become cyclic (detected during forest processing), they are reported as cycle errors with the full backtrace for user understanding.\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":10,"cache_creation_input_tokens":1982,"cache_read_input_tokens":52395,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":1982},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"f881b69a-ae4e-4ac1-be14-81f4942f79df","uuid":"98a44a39-744e-45e3-8f13-d999697e99a1"}

compiler's trait obligation solver implements a sophisticated system for resolving trait bounds and detecting unsatisfied trait constraints. The system follows a pipeline architecture with clear separation of concerns.\\n\\n## Obligation Forest Foundation\\nThe `ObligationForest` (compiler/rustc_data_structures/src/obligation_forest/mod.rs) provides the core data structure for managing trait obligations. It maintains a forest of obligation trees where each node represents a pending obligation. The forest supports three processing results: Unchanged (ambiguous), Changed with sub-obligations, and Error. The state machine includes states: Pending -> Success -> Waiting -> Done, or Error. This enables efficient batch processing while tracking obligation dependencies.\\n\\n## Fulfillment and Obligation Registration\\nThe `FulfillmentContext` (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/fulfill.rs) wraps the ObligationForest for the old trait solver. When obligations are registered via `ObligationCtxt::register_obligation` (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/engine.rs), they become `PendingPredicateObligation` nodes containing the predicate, parameter environment, and recursion depth. The context implements `ObligationProcessor` to handle obligation processing callbacks.\\n\\n## Trait Selection Pipeline\\nThe `SelectionContext` (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/mod.rs) is the central orchestrator for trait resolution. The selection process follows a well-defined pipeline:\\n\\n1. **Candidate Assembly**: The `assemble_candidates` method (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/candidate_assembly.rs) gathers all possible trait implementations from:\\n   - Trait aliases\\n   - User-defined implementations\\n   - Caller bounds and where-clauses\\n   - Builtin implementations (Copy, Clone, Sized, etc.)\\n   - Auto-traits\\n   - Projection candidates (associated types)\\n\\n2. **Matching**: The `MatchAgainstFreshVars` type relation (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/_match.rs) tests whether candidate trait references match the obligation. It performs type unification on freshened types to determine if an impl could satisfy the obligation.\\n\\n3. **Confirmation**: The `confirm_candidate` method (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/confirmation.rs) unifies the trait reference with the obligation and produces an `ImplSource` that represents the selected implementation. For user-defined impls, it recursively generates sub-obligations for where-clause bounds.\\n\\n## Specialization and Impl Matching\\nThe specialization system (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/specialize/mod.rs) enforces impl consistency rules. The `OverlapError` structure handles cases where multiple impls could apply. The specialization graph (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/specialize/specialization_graph.rs) organizes impls by their specificity, ensuring that more specific implementations take precedence.\\n\\n## Associated Type Projection\\nThe projection system (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/project.rs) resolves associated types during trait selection. It defines `ProjectionObligation` types and `ProjectionCandidate` sources including parameter environment bounds, trait definitions, object types, and selections. This system integrates with the main trait solver to handle complex generic types with associated type constraints.\\n\\n## Error Reporting\\nWhen obligations cannot be satisfied, the error reporting system provides detailed diagnostics:\\n\\n- `report_selection_error` (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/error_reporting/traits/fulfillment_errors.rs) generates the primary error message, handling multiple error categories including Unimplemented, Unsupported, and TraitNotObjectSafe\\n- The error reporting context (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/error_reporting/traits/mod.rs) manages candidate similarity analysis and provides contextual information\\n- The suggestions module (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/error_reporting/traits/suggestions.rs) offers actionable fixes\\n\\n## Type System Integration\\nThe trait system integrates with the broader type system through several key types:\\n\\n- `ObligationCause` (compiler/rustc_middle/src/traits/mod.rs) provides attribution for why obligations exist, including the source span and obligation cause code\\n- `FulfillmentError` tracks failed obligations with their error codes and root cause information\\n- `Obligation<T>` (compiler/rustc_infer/src/traits/mod.rs) is the generic container for any goal to prove, including recursion depth tracking for termination\\n\\nThe unified interface allows the same machinery to handle trait predicates, projection predicates, and well-formedness constraints. When obligations become cyclic (detected during forest processing), they are reported as cycle errors with the full backtrace for user understanding.\"\n   224→}\n   225→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. \"compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/error_reporting/traits/fulfillment_errors.rs\",\n      \"symbol\": \"report_selection_error\"\n    }\n  ],\n  \"text\": \"The Rust compiler's trait obligation solver implements a sophisticated system for resolving trait bounds and detecting unsatisfied trait constraints. The system follows a pipeline architecture with clear separation of concerns.\\n\\n## Obligation Forest Foundation\\nThe `ObligationForest` (compiler/rustc_data_structures/src/obligation_forest/mod.rs) provides the core data structure for managing trait obligations. It maintains a forest of obligation trees where each node represents a pending obligation. The forest supports three processing results: Unchanged (ambiguous), Changed with sub-obligations, and Error. The state machine includes states: Pending -> Success -> Waiting -> Done, or Error. This enables efficient batch processing while tracking obligation dependencies.\\n\\n## Fulfillment and Obligation Registration\\nThe `FulfillmentContext` (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/fulfill.rs) wraps the ObligationForest for the old trait solver. When obligations are registered via `ObligationCtxt::register_obligation` (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/engine.rs), they become `PendingPredicateObligation` nodes containing the predicate, parameter environment, and recursion depth. The context implements `ObligationProcessor` to handle obligation processing callbacks.\\n\\n## Trait Selection Pipeline\\nThe `SelectionContext` (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/mod.rs) is the central orchestrator for trait resolution. The selection process follows a well-defined pipeline:\\n\\n1. **Candidate Assembly**: The `assemble_candidates` method (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/candidate_assembly.rs) gathers all possible trait implementations from:\\n   - Trait aliases\\n   - User-defined implementations\\n   - Caller bounds and where-clauses\\n   - Builtin implementations (Copy, Clone, Sized, etc.)\\n   - Auto-traits\\n   - Projection candidates (associated types)\\n\\n2. **Matching**: The `MatchAgainstFreshVars` type relation (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/_match.rs) tests whether candidate trait references match the obligation. It performs type unification on freshened types to determine if an impl could satisfy the obligation.\\n\\n3. **Confirmation**: The `confirm_candidate` method (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/confirmation.rs) unifies the trait reference with the obligation and produces an `ImplSource` that represents the selected implementation. For user-defined impls, it recursively generates sub-obligations for where-clause bounds.\\n\\n## Specialization and Impl Matching\\nThe specialization system (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/specialize/mod.rs) enforces impl consistency rules. The `OverlapError` structure handles cases where multiple impls could apply. The specialization graph (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/specialize/specialization_graph.rs) organizes impls by their specificity, ensuring that more specific implementations take precedence.\\n\\n## Associated Type Projection\\nThe projection system (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/project.rs) resolves associated types during trait selection. It defines `ProjectionObligation` types and `ProjectionCandidate` sources including parameter environment bounds, trait definitions, object types, and selections. This system integrates with the main trait solver to handle complex generic types with associated type constraints.\\n\\n## Error Reporting\\nWhen obligations cannot be satisfied, the error reporting system provides detailed diagnostics:\\n\\n- `report_selection_error` (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/error_reporting/traits/fulfillment_errors.rs) generates the primary error message, handling multiple error categories including Unimplemented, Unsupported, and TraitNotObjectSafe\\n- The error reporting context (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/error_reporting/traits/mod.rs) manages candidate similarity analysis and provides contextual information\\n- The suggestions module (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/error_reporting/traits/suggestions.rs) offers actionable fixes\\n\\n## Type System Integration\\nThe trait system integrates with the broader type system through several key types:\\n\\n- `ObligationCause` (compiler/rustc_middle/src/traits/mod.rs) provides attribution for why obligations exist, including the source span and obligation cause code\\n- `FulfillmentError` tracks failed obligations with their error codes and root cause information\\n- `Obligation<T>` (compiler/rustc_infer/src/traits/mod.rs) is the generic container for any goal to prove, including recursion depth tracking for termination\\n\\nThe unified interface allows the same machinery to handle trait predicates, projection predicates, and well-formedness constraints. When obligations become cyclic (detected during forest processing), they are reported as cycle errors with the full backtrace for user understanding.\"\n}\n","numLines":225,"startLine":1,"totalLines":225}}}

solver implements a sophisticated system for resolving trait bounds and detecting unsatisfied trait constraints. The system follows a pipeline architecture with clear separation of concerns.\\n\\n## Obligation Forest Foundation\\nThe `ObligationForest` (compiler/rustc_data_structures/src/obligation_forest/mod.rs) provides the core data structure for managing trait obligations. It maintains a forest of obligation trees where each node represents a pending obligation. The forest supports three processing results: Unchanged (ambiguous), Changed with sub-obligations, and Error. The state machine includes states: Pending -> Success -> Waiting -> Done, or Error. This enables efficient batch processing while tracking obligation dependencies.\\n\\n## Fulfillment and Obligation Registration\\nThe `FulfillmentContext` (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/fulfill.rs) wraps the ObligationForest for the old trait solver. When obligations are registered via `ObligationCtxt::register_obligation` (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/engine.rs), they become `PendingPredicateObligation` nodes containing the predicate, parameter environment, and recursion depth. The context implements `ObligationProcessor` to handle obligation processing callbacks.\\n\\n## Trait Selection Pipeline\\nThe `SelectionContext` (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/mod.rs) is the central orchestrator for trait resolution. The selection process follows a well-defined pipeline:\\n\\n1. **Candidate Assembly**: The `assemble_candidates` method (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/candidate_assembly.rs) gathers all possible trait implementations from:\\n   - Trait aliases\\n   - User-defined implementations\\n   - Caller bounds and where-clauses\\n   - Builtin implementations (Copy, Clone, Sized, etc.)\\n   - Auto-traits\\n   - Projection candidates (associated types)\\n\\n2. **Matching**: The `MatchAgainstFreshVars` type relation (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/_match.rs) tests whether candidate trait references match the obligation. It performs type unification on freshened types to determine if an impl could satisfy the obligation.\\n\\n3. **Confirmation**: The `confirm_candidate` method (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/confirmation.rs) unifies the trait reference with the obligation and produces an `ImplSource` that represents the selected implementation. For user-defined impls, it recursively generates sub-obligations for where-clause bounds.\\n\\n## Specialization and Impl Matching\\nThe specialization system (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/specialize/mod.rs) enforces impl consistency rules. The `OverlapError` structure handles cases where multiple impls could apply. The specialization graph (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/specialize/specialization_graph.rs) organizes impls by their specificity, ensuring that more specific implementations take precedence.\\n\\n## Associated Type Projection\\nThe projection system (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/project.rs) resolves associated types during trait selection. It defines `ProjectionObligation` types and `ProjectionCandidate` sources including parameter environment bounds, trait definitions, object types, and selections. This system integrates with the main trait solver to handle complex generic types with associated type constraints.\\n\\n## Error Reporting\\nWhen obligations cannot be satisfied, the error reporting system provides detailed diagnostics:\\n\\n- `report_selection_error` (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/error_reporting/traits/fulfillment_errors.rs) generates the primary error message, handling multiple error categories including Unimplemented, Unsupported, and TraitNotObjectSafe\\n- The error reporting context (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/error_reporting/traits/mod.rs) manages candidate similarity analysis and provides contextual information\\n- The suggestions module (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/error_reporting/traits/suggestions.rs) offers actionable fixes\\n\\n## Type System Integration\\nThe trait system integrates with the broader type system through several key types:\\n\\n- `ObligationCause` (compiler/rustc_middle/src/traits/mod.rs) provides attribution for why obligations exist, including the source span and obligation cause code\\n- `FulfillmentError` tracks failed obligations with their error codes and root cause information\\n- `Obligation<T>` (compiler/rustc_infer/src/traits/mod.rs) is the generic container for any goal to prove, including recursion depth tracking for termination\\n\\nThe unified interface allows the same machinery to handle trait predicates, projection predicates, and well-formedness constraints. When obligations become cyclic (detected during forest processing), they are reported as cycle errors with the full backtrace for user understanding.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[{"oldStart":143,"oldLines":6,"newStart":143,"newLines":11,"lines":["     },","     {","       \"repo\": \"rust-lang/rust\",","+      \"path\": \"compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/normalize.rs\",","+      \"symbol\": \"normalize_with_depth\"","+    },","+    {","+      \"repo\": \"rust-lang/rust\",","       \"path\": \"compiler/rustc_middle/src/traits/mod.rs\",","       \"symbol\": \"ObligationCause\"","     },"]}],"userModified":false,"replaceAll":false}}

The system follows a pipeline architecture with clear separation of concerns.\\n\\n## Obligation Forest Foundation\\nThe `ObligationForest` (compiler/rustc_data_structures/src/obligation_forest/mod.rs) provides the core data structure for managing trait obligations. It maintains a forest of obligation trees where each node represents a pending obligation. The forest supports three processing results: Unchanged (ambiguous), Changed with sub-obligations, and Error. The state machine includes states: Pending -> Success -> Waiting -> Done, or Error. This enables efficient batch processing while tracking obligation dependencies.\\n\\n## Fulfillment and Obligation Registration\\nThe `FulfillmentContext` (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/fulfill.rs) wraps the ObligationForest for the old trait solver. The context implements `ObligationProcessor` to handle obligation processing callbacks.\\n\\n## Trait Selection Pipeline\\nThe `SelectionContext` (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/mod.rs) is the central orchestrator for trait resolution. It performs type unification on freshened types to determine if an impl could satisfy the obligation.\\n\\n3. **Confirmation**: The `confirm_candidate` method (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/confirmation.rs) unifies the trait reference with the obligation and produces an `ImplSource` that represents the selected implementation. For user-defined impls, it recursively generates sub-obligations for where-clause bounds.\\n\\n## Specialization and Impl Matching\\nThe specialization system (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/specialize/mod.rs) enforces impl consistency rules. The `OverlapError` structure handles cases where multiple impls could apply. It defines `ProjectionObligation` types and `ProjectionCandidate` sources including parameter environment bounds, trait definitions, object types, and selections. This system integrates with the main trait solver to handle complex generic types with associated type constraints.\\n\\n## Error Reporting\\nWhen obligations cannot be satisfied, the error reporting system provides detailed diagnostics:\\n\\n- `report_selection_error` (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/error_reporting/traits/fulfillment_errors.rs) generates the primary error message, handling multiple error categories including Unimplemented, Unsupported, and TraitNotObjectSafe\\n- The error reporting context (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/error_reporting/traits/mod.rs) manages candidate similarity analysis and provides contextual information\\n- The suggestions module (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/error_reporting/traits/suggestions.rs) offers actionable fixes\\n\\n## Type System Integration\\nThe trait system integrates with the broader type system through several key types:\\n\\n- `ObligationCause` (compiler/rustc_middle/src/traits/mod.rs) provides attribution for why obligations exist, including the source span and obligation cause code\\n- `FulfillmentError` tracks failed obligations with their error codes and root cause information\\n- `Obligation<T>` (compiler/rustc_infer/src/traits/mod.rs) is the generic container for any goal to prove, including recursion depth tracking for termination\\n\\nThe unified interface allows the same machinery to handle trait predicates, projection predicates, and well-formedness constraints. solver implements a sophisticated system for resolving trait bounds and detecting unsatisfied trait constraints. The system follows a pipeline architecture with clear separation of concerns.\\n\\n## Obligation Forest Foundation\\nThe `ObligationForest` (compiler/rustc_data_structures/src/obligation_forest/mod.rs) provides the core data structure for managing trait obligations. It maintains a forest of obligation trees where each node represents a pending obligation. The forest supports three processing results: Unchanged (ambiguous), Changed with sub-obligations, and Error. The state machine includes states: Pending -> Success -> Waiting -> Done, or Error. This enables efficient batch processing while tracking obligation dependencies.\\n\\n## Fulfillment and Obligation Registration\\nThe `FulfillmentContext` (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/fulfill.rs) wraps the ObligationForest for the old trait solver. When obligations are registered via `ObligationCtxt::register_obligation` (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/engine.rs), they become `PendingPredicateObligation` nodes containing the predicate, parameter environment, and recursion depth. The context implements `ObligationProcessor` to handle obligation processing callbacks.\\n\\n## Trait Selection Pipeline\\nThe `SelectionContext` (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/mod.rs) is the central orchestrator for trait resolution. The selection process follows a well-defined pipeline:\\n\\n1. **Candidate Assembly**: The `assemble_candidates` method (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/candidate_assembly.rs) gathers all possible trait implementations from:\\n   - Trait aliases\\n   - User-defined implementations\\n   - Caller bounds and where-clauses\\n   - Builtin implementations (Copy, Clone, Sized, etc.)\\n   - Auto-traits\\n   - Projection candidates (associated types)\\n\\n2. **Matching**: The `MatchAgainstFreshVars` type relation (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/_match.rs) tests whether candidate trait references match the obligation. It performs type unification on freshened types to determine if an impl could satisfy the obligation.\\n\\n3. **Confirmation**: The `confirm_candidate` method (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/confirmation.rs) unifies the trait reference with the obligation and produces an `ImplSource` that represents the selected implementation. For user-defined impls, it recursively generates sub-obligations for where-clause bounds.\\n\\n## Specialization and Impl Matching\\nThe specialization system (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/specialize/mod.rs) enforces impl consistency rules. The `OverlapError` structure handles cases where multiple impls could apply. The specialization graph (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/specialize/specialization_graph.rs) organizes impls by their specificity, ensuring that more specific implementations take precedence.\\n\\n## Associated Type Projection\\nThe projection system (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/project.rs) resolves associated types during trait selection. It defines `ProjectionObligation` types and `ProjectionCandidate` sources including parameter environment bounds, trait definitions, object types, and selections. This system integrates with the main trait solver to handle complex generic types with associated type constraints.\\n\\n## Error Reporting\\nWhen obligations cannot be satisfied, the error reporting system provides detailed diagnostics:\\n\\n- `report_selection_error` (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/error_reporting/traits/fulfillment_errors.rs) generates the primary error message, handling multiple error categories including Unimplemented, Unsupported, and TraitNotObjectSafe\\n- The error reporting context (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/error_reporting/traits/mod.rs) manages candidate similarity analysis and provides contextual information\\n- The suggestions module (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/error_reporting/traits/suggestions.rs) offers actionable fixes\\n\\n## Type System Integration\\nThe trait system integrates with the broader type system through several key types:\\n\\n- `ObligationCause` (compiler/rustc_middle/src/traits/mod.rs) provides attribution for why obligations exist, including the source span and obligation cause code\\n- `FulfillmentError` tracks failed obligations with their error codes and root cause information\\n- `Obligation<T>` (compiler/rustc_infer/src/traits/mod.rs) is the generic container for any goal to prove, including recursion depth tracking for termination\\n\\nThe unified interface allows the same machinery to handle trait predicates, projection predicates, and well-formedness constraints. When obligations become cyclic (detected during forest processing), they are reported as cycle errors with the full backtrace for user understanding.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[{"oldStart":234,"oldLines":5,"newStart":234,"newLines":5,"lines":["       \"symbol\": \"report_selection_error\"","     }","   ],","-  \"text\": \"The Rust compiler's trait obligation solver implements a sophisticated system for resolving trait bounds and detecting unsatisfied trait constraints. The system follows a pipeline architecture with clear separation of concerns.\\n\\n## Obligation Forest Foundation\\nThe `ObligationForest` (compiler/rustc_data_structures/src/obligation_forest/mod.rs) provides the core data structure for managing trait obligations. It maintains a forest of obligation trees where each node represents a pending obligation. The forest supports three processing results: Unchanged (ambiguous), Changed with sub-obligations, and Error. The state machine includes states: Pending -> Success -> Waiting -> Done, or Error. This enables efficient batch processing while tracking obligation dependencies.\\n\\n## Fulfillment and Obligation Registration\\nThe `FulfillmentContext` (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/fulfill.rs) wraps the ObligationForest for the old trait solver. When obligations are registered via `ObligationCtxt::register_obligation` (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/engine.rs), they become `PendingPredicateObligation` nodes containing the predicate, parameter environment, and recursion depth. The context implements `ObligationProcessor` to handle obligation processing callbacks.\\n\\n## Trait Selection Pipeline\\nThe `SelectionContext` (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/mod.rs) is the central orchestrator for trait resolution. The selection process follows a well-defined pipeline:\\n\\n1. **Candidate Assembly**: The `assemble_candidates` method (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/candidate_assembly.rs) gathers all possible trait implementations from:\\n   - Trait aliases\\n   - User-defined implementations\\n   - Caller bounds and where-clauses\\n   - Builtin implementations (Copy, Clone, Sized, etc.)\\n   - Auto-traits\\n   - Projection candidates (associated types)\\n\\n2. **Matching**: The `MatchAgainstFreshVars` type relation (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/_match.rs) tests whether candidate trait references match the obligation. It performs type unification on freshened types to determine if an impl could satisfy the obligation.\\n\\n3. **Confirmation**: The `confirm_candidate` method (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/confirmation.rs) unifies the trait reference with the obligation and produces an `ImplSource` that represents the selected implementation. For user-defined impls, it recursively generates sub-obligations for where-clause bounds.\\n\\n## Specialization and Impl Matching\\nThe specialization system (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/specialize/mod.rs) enforces impl consistency rules. The `OverlapError` structure handles cases where multiple impls could apply. The specialization graph (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/specialize/specialization_graph.rs) organizes impls by their specificity, ensuring that more specific implementations take precedence.\\n\\n## Associated Type Projection\\nThe projection system (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/project.rs) resolves associated types during trait selection. It defines `ProjectionObligation` types and `ProjectionCandidate` sources including parameter environment bounds, trait definitions, object types, and selections. This system integrates with the main trait solver to handle complex generic types with associated type constraints.\\n\\n## Error Reporting\\nWhen obligations cannot be satisfied, the error reporting system provides detailed diagnostics:\\n\\n- `report_selection_error` (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/error_reporting/traits/fulfillment_errors.rs) generates the primary error message, handling multiple error categories including Unimplemented, Unsupported, and TraitNotObjectSafe\\n- The error reporting context (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/error_reporting/traits/mod.rs) manages candidate similarity analysis and provides contextual information\\n- The suggestions module (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/error_reporting/traits/suggestions.rs) offers actionable fixes\\n\\n## Type System Integration\\nThe trait system integrates with the broader type system through several key types:\\n\\n- `ObligationCause` (compiler/rustc_middle/src/traits/mod.rs) provides attribution for why obligations exist, including the source span and obligation cause code\\n- `FulfillmentError` tracks failed obligations with their error codes and root cause information\\n- `Obligation<T>` (compiler/rustc_infer/src/traits/mod.rs) is the generic container for any goal to prove, including recursion depth tracking for termination\\n\\nThe unified interface allows the same machinery to handle trait predicates, projection predicates, and well-formedness constraints. When obligations become cyclic (detected during forest processing), they are reported as cycle errors with the full backtrace for user understanding.\"","+  \"text\": \"The Rust compiler's trait obligation solver implements a sophisticated system for resolving trait bounds and detecting unsatisfied trait constraints. The system follows a pipeline architecture with clear separation of concerns.\\n\\n## Obligation Forest Foundation\\nThe `ObligationForest` (compiler/rustc_data_structures/src/obligation_forest/mod.rs) provides the core data structure for managing trait obligations. It maintains a forest of obligation trees where each node represents a pending obligation. The forest supports three processing results: Unchanged (ambiguous), Changed with sub-obligations, and Error. The state machine includes states: Pending -> Success -> Waiting -> Done, or Error. This enables efficient batch processing while tracking obligation dependencies.\\n\\n## Fulfillment and Obligation Registration\\nThe `FulfillmentContext` (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/fulfill.rs) wraps the ObligationForest for the old trait solver. When obligations are registered via `ObligationCtxt::register_obligation` (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/engine.rs), they become `PendingPredicateObligation` nodes containing the predicate, parameter environment, and recursion depth. The context implements `ObligationProcessor` to handle obligation processing callbacks.\\n\\n## Trait Selection Pipeline\\nThe `SelectionContext` (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/mod.rs) is the central orchestrator for trait resolution. The selection process follows a well-defined pipeline:\\n\\n1. **Candidate Assembly**: The `assemble_candidates` method (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/candidate_assembly.rs) gathers all possible trait implementations from:\\n   - Trait aliases\\n   - User-defined implementations\\n   - Caller bounds and where-clauses\\n   - Builtin implementations (Copy, Clone, Sized, etc.)\\n   - Auto-traits\\n   - Projection candidates (associated types)\\n\\n2. **Matching**: The `MatchAgainstFreshVars` type relation (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/_match.rs) tests whether candidate trait references match the obligation. It performs type unification on freshened types to determine if an impl could satisfy the obligation.\\n\\n3. **Confirmation**: The `confirm_candidate` method (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/confirmation.rs) unifies the trait reference with the obligation and produces an `ImplSource` that represents the selected implementation. For user-defined impls, it recursively generates sub-obligations for where-clause bounds.\\n\\n## Specialization and Impl Matching\\nThe specialization system (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/specialize/mod.rs) enforces impl consistency rules. The `OverlapError` structure handles cases where multiple impls could apply. The specialization graph (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/specialize/specialization_graph.rs) organizes impls by their specificity, ensuring that more specific implementations take precedence.\\n\\n## Associated Type Projection and Normalization\\nThe projection system (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/project.rs) resolves associated types during trait selection. It defines `ProjectionObligation` types and `ProjectionCandidate` sources including parameter environment bounds, trait definitions, object types, and selections. This system integrates with the main trait solver to handle complex generic types with associated type constraints.\\n\\nNormalization (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/normalize.rs) deeply replaces all aliases and associated types with their concrete implementations using the `normalize_with_depth` function. This is crucial for trait resolution as it transforms projection types like `<T as Trait>::Associated` into the actual implementing type, enabling proper obligation matching and solving.\\n\\n## Error Reporting\\nWhen obligations cannot be satisfied, the error reporting system provides detailed diagnostics:\\n\\n- `report_selection_error` (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/error_reporting/traits/fulfillment_errors.rs) generates the primary error message, handling multiple error categories including Unimplemented, Unsupported, and TraitNotObjectSafe\\n- The error reporting context (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/error_reporting/traits/mod.rs) manages candidate similarity analysis and provides contextual information\\n- The suggestions module (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/error_reporting/traits/suggestions.rs) offers actionable fixes\\n\\n## Type System Integration\\nThe trait system integrates with the broader type system through several key types:\\n\\n- `ObligationCause` (compiler/rustc_middle/src/traits/mod.rs) provides attribution for why obligations exist, including the source span and obligation cause code\\n- `FulfillmentError` tracks failed obligations with their error codes and root cause information\\n- `Obligation<T>` (compiler/rustc_infer/src/traits/mod.rs) is the generic container for any goal to prove, including recursion depth tracking for termination\\n\\nThe unified interface allows the same machinery to handle trait predicates, projection predicates, and well-formedness constraints. When obligations become cyclic (detected during forest processing), they are reported as cycle errors with the full backtrace for user understanding.\""," }"]}],"userModified":false,"replaceAll":false}}
